### ⚙ Tool call: `Edit`

```json
{
  "replace_all": false,
  "file_path": "/workspace/CLAUDE.md",
  "old_string": "## Development archive (`development/`)",
  "new_string": "## Testing\n\nThere is a pytest harness under `tests/` (built 2026-07; design in\n`development/2026-07-04-test-harness/SPEC.md`). Run it with `./run-tests` (wrapper over\npytest): `./run-tests --fast` is the offline inner loop; `./run-tests` adds the live tier;\n`--llm` gives terse machine-parseable output; `--coverage`, `--update-goldens`, and\n`--record` do what they say. Tiers are pytest marks: `unit`, `integration`, `e2e`, `live`,\n`render`, `email`, `slow`. **When you change the program, add/adjust the appropriate tests in\nthe same change** (this project does not do TDD — tests follow the change).\n\nNon-obvious things the harness relies on:\n- **The script is imported, not re-parsed.** `tests/conftest.py` loads the extension-less\n  `pantheon-sitehealth-emails` via `importlib`/`SourceFileLoader` (fixture `psh`). Argparse was\n  refactored into `build_arg_parser()`/`parse_args()`; `sc.options` is set by the caller, so a\n  test sets it (the `reset_sc` autouse fixture does) before calling functions. `MPLBACKEND=Agg`\n  must be set before the load (conftest does this) because the module imports `matplotlib.pyplot`\n  at the top.\n- **Two mock seams.** All Pantheon/WP/Drush I/O funnels through `run_terminus()` — monkeypatch it\n  for in-process tests, or use the PATH-shim fake `terminus` (`tests/shims/terminus`, record/replay)\n  for full subprocess e2e. The `php inline-styles.php` CSS inliner uses **real php**.\n- **Safety interlock.** `run_program()` in conftest is the only sanctioned way to run the program\n  in a subprocess; it raises `ForbiddenFlagError` if `--all`/`-a`/`--for-real` appear. Never\n  bypass it. Tests use only `its-wws-test1`/`its-wws-test2`, read-only.\n- **Offline e2e determinism.** The shim-backed run uses `tests/fixtures/config/minimal.toml`,\n  seeded traffic, `--date 2026-03-31` (a mid-year date avoids the U-M contract-year-end path),\n  and a `domain:list` fixture reduced to the platform domain (so no live DNS). Golden snapshots\n  normalize the volatile `make_msgid` CIDs; refresh with `./run-tests --update-goldens`. Refresh\n  terminus fixtures with `./run-tests --record` (trims org list to the test site, scrubs emails).\n- **The reusable (non-UMich) path had latent bugs** that production never hit because U-M always\n  runs with the UMich plugin enabled. Several U-M-specific code paths in the core script are not\n  yet behind the `[UMich].enabled` flag; the planned refactor should move them out. When adding\n  code, keep institution-specific logic behind config flags / the `umich` plugin+check packages.\n\n## Development archive (`development/`)"
}
```

## Assistant

Now the dev-facing `tests/README.md`:

### ⚙ Tool call: `Write`

```json
{
  "file_path": "/workspace/tests/README.md",
  "content": "# Test harness for `pantheon-sitehealth-emails`\n\nDesign and rationale: [`../development/2026-07-04-test-harness/SPEC.md`](../development/2026-07-04-test-harness/SPEC.md).\nThis README is the practical, day-to-day reference.\n\n## Running\n\nUse the `./run-tests` wrapper (from the repo root):\n\n| Command | What it does |\n|---|---|\n| `./run-tests` | All tiers, including `live` (needs Terminus auth + network). |\n| `./run-tests --fast` | Offline subset: `-m \"not live and not slow\"`. The inner loop. |\n| `./run-tests --llm` | Terse, machine-parseable summary (`LLM_SUMMARY …` + `FAILED <nodeid>`). |\n| `./run-tests --coverage` | Report coverage (no gate; **in-process tiers only**, see below). |\n| `./run-tests --update-goldens` | Refresh the rendered-report snapshots after an intended change. |\n| `./run-tests --record` | Re-record the terminus fixtures from the live test site (read-only). |\n\nExtra args pass through to pytest: `./run-tests -m e2e`, `./run-tests -k drush`, `./run-tests tests/unit`.\n\nFirst-time setup:\n\n```bash\nuv pip install .[test]\npython -m playwright install --with-deps chromium   # render tier; --with-deps needs sudo\n```\n\nIf Chromium isn't installed, the `render` test **skips** with the exact setup command (it does\nnot fail).\n\n## Layout\n\n```\ntests/\n  conftest.py        # fixtures + the run_program() safety interlock (start here)\n  fixtures/\n    config/          # minimal.toml (plugins off) + full.toml (plugins on); self-contained\n    terminus/        # recorded terminus responses, keyed by a hash of the argv\n  shims/terminus     # fake terminus (record/replay) put on PATH for e2e\n  tools/record.py    # re-records + trims/scrubs the terminus fixtures\n  __snapshots__/     # syrupy golden baselines (normalized rendered report)\n  unit/              # pure/in-process helpers + Hypothesis + the interlock test\n  integration/       # monkeypatched run_terminus, temp DB, check hooks, bug regressions\n  e2e/               # full subprocess run via the shim; artifact + golden assertions\n  live/              # real terminus, read-only (marked live+slow)\n  render/            # headless-browser render of the report\n  email/             # deferred GMail round-trip scaffold (skipped)\n```\n\n## Marks / tiers\n\n`unit`, `integration`, `e2e`, `live`, `render`, `email`, `slow`. `--fast` excludes `live` and\n`slow`. Choose the relevant subset for a change (e.g. a Drupal-check edit → `-m \"unit or integration\" -k drush`\nplus the Drupal live/e2e cases).\n\n## Writing a test\n\n- Get the program module from the `psh` fixture (it's imported once; don't import it yourself).\n- `sc.options` is pre-set by the autouse `reset_sc` fixture (which also isolates `sc` global\n  state between tests). Request `reset_sc` if you need the `sc` module object.\n- For in-process Pantheon calls, `monkeypatch.setattr(psh, \"run_terminus\", fake)`.\n- To run the whole program, use the `program_runner` fixture (or the module-scoped\n  `rendered_report` fixture, which runs the offline pipeline once and exposes the artifacts).\n  **Never** invoke the program except through `run_program` — it enforces the `--all`/`--for-real`\n  interlock.\n- Temp DB: the `temp_db` fixture gives a fresh sqlite engine + session + the ORM models.\n\n## Determinism notes\n\n- The offline e2e uses `minimal.toml`, seeded traffic, and `--date 2026-03-31` (mid-year, to\n  avoid the U-M contract-year-end code path). The `domain:list` fixture is reduced to the platform\n  domain so replay makes **no live DNS** calls.\n- Golden snapshots normalize the volatile `make_msgid` CIDs (`cid:…` → `cid:NORMALIZED`). The\n  matplotlib chart/gauge PNGs are attached by CID and not byte-compared. `MPLBACKEND=Agg` is\n  forced before the module loads.\n- Regenerate golden snapshots only deliberately: `./run-tests --update-goldens`, then review the diff.\n\n## Recording / refreshing terminus fixtures\n\n`./run-tests --record` runs the program live against `its-wws-test1` (read-only) with the shim in\nrecord mode, then trims `org:site:list` to the test site, reduces `domain:list` to the platform\ndomain, and scrubs `site:team:list` emails to `test-owner{1,2}@umich.edu`. Review the diff before\ncommitting; each fixture carries a `recorded` date.\n\n## Coverage\n\n`--coverage` measures the **in-process** tiers (unit/integration). The e2e/live tiers run the\nprogram in a subprocess that pytest-cov does not see unless `COVERAGE_PROCESS_START` +\n`coverage.process_startup()` plumbing is added (not wired yet). So the reported number reflects\nin-process code, not whole-program coverage. There is no coverage gate by design.\n"
}
```

```
File created successfully at: /workspace/tests/README.md (file state is current in your context — no need to Read it back)
```

### ⚙ Tool call: `Write`

```json
{
  "file_path": "/workspace/development/2026-07-04-test-harness/add-tests-for-change.prompt.md",
  "content": "# Prompt: add tests for a change\n\nReusable prompt for keeping the suite current (this project adds tests *with* each change, not\nTDD-first). Run this after making a code change, or fold it into the change's own prompt.\n\n---\n\nI just changed `<describe the change / paste the diff>`.\n\nDesign and implement the appropriate tests for it, following the existing harness in `tests/`\n(see `tests/README.md` and `development/2026-07-04-test-harness/SPEC.md`):\n\n1. Pick the right tier(s) by what changed:\n   - pure/in-process logic → `tests/unit/` (add a Hypothesis property test if the function is\n     pure and has an invariant worth fuzzing);\n   - anything going through `run_terminus`/WP/Drush, the DB, or a check hook → `tests/integration/`\n     (monkeypatch `run_terminus`, use `temp_db`);\n   - a change visible in the rendered report or the full pipeline → extend the `e2e` run and the\n     `golden` snapshot; if it changes real Pantheon interaction, add/adjust a `live` case;\n   - a rendering/CSS/template change → the `render` tier.\n2. Reuse the existing fixtures (`psh`, `reset_sc`, `temp_db`, `program_runner`, `rendered_report`,\n   `minimal_config`). Never invoke the program except via `run_program` (the `--all`/`--for-real`\n   interlock).\n3. ## What landed
```

**Source changes (minimal, behavior-preserving):**
- **Seam refactor** — arg parsing wrapped in `build_arg_parser()`/`parse_args()`, `sc.options` set in `__main__`. Verified: `--help` byte-identical, module now imports cleanly under any `sys.argv`, same parsed namespace.
- **Bug fixes (4, each covered by a test):**
  1. `terminus()` session-expiry retry (tuple `.push`/`del` crash) — spec bug #1
  2. `check/umich` `sc.console(...)` not-callable — spec bug #2
  3. **`contacts` UnboundLocalError** — *newly discovered*, non-UMich path
  4. **unguarded `if True:` U-M annual-billing block** (`KeyError('UMich')`) — *newly discovered*, now behind the `[UMich].enabled` flag

Bugs #3/#4 are on the reusable (non-U-M) path that production never hits because U-M always runs the UMich plugin — exactly the reusability the project targets. They're regressed by the offline e2e (which renders under the plugin-disabled config).

**Harness (`tests/`):** conftest (importlib module loader with `MPLBACKEND=Agg`, `sc`-state reset, `temp_db`, config fixtures, the `run_program` `--all`/`--for-real` interlock, `--llm` reporter), a record/replay `terminus` shim, `minimal.toml`/`full.toml`, scrubbed terminus fixtures, golden snapshots, the `./run-tests` wrapper, and `tools/record.py`. One smoke test per tier (unit, integration, e2e, golden, property, live, render, email-skipped) plus regressions and the interlock test.

**Acceptance criteria** — all met: `--fast` green offline; full run green incl. live Terminus; `--llm` emits `LLM_SUMMARY`; `--coverage` reports (no gate); `--update-goldens` round-trips; interlock refuses forbidden flags; docs updated (README Testing section, CLAUDE.md, `tests/README.md`, pyproject); seam byte-identity recorded in `HANDOFF.md`.

## Two things for you

1. **Render tier needs a one-time sudo step** I can't run (no passwordless sudo here). The test *skips* with the command until then. To enable it:
   ```
   ! python -m playwright install --with-deps chromium
   ```
   Then `./run-tests --fast` will run it instead of skipping.

2. **Scope note:** I fixed 2 bugs beyond the spec's 2, because the non-UMich render path was completely broken (blocking all offline testing) and fixing it directly serves the project's reusability goal. Details and remaining U-M-coupling follow-ups are in `development/2026-07-04-test-harness/HANDOFF.md`. If you'd rather I hadn't touched #3/#4, say so and I'll reconsider — but the offline e2e/golden/render tiers depend on them.

## User

<command-message>code-review</command-message>
<command-name>/code-review</command-name>
<command-args>high</command-args>

## User

`high effort → 3+5 angles × 6 candidates → 1-vote verify (recall-biased) → ≤10 findings`

You are reviewing for **recall** at high effort: catch every real bug a careful
reviewer would catch in one sitting. At this level, catching real bugs matters
more than avoiding false positives. Err on the side of surfacing.

## Phase 0 — Gather the diff

Run `git diff @{upstream}...HEAD` (or `git diff main...HEAD` / `git diff HEAD~1`
if there's no upstream) to get the unified diff under review. If there are
uncommitted changes, or the range diff is empty, also run `git diff HEAD` and
include the working-tree changes in scope — the review often runs before the
commit. If a PR number, branch name, or file path was passed as an argument,
review that target instead. Treat this diff as the review scope.

## Phase 1 — Find candidates (3 correctness angles + 3 cleanup angles + 1 altitude angle + 1 conventions angle, up to 6 each)

Run **8 independent finder angles** via the Agent tool. Each
surfaces **up to 6 candidate findings** with `file`, `line`, a one-line
`summary`, and a concrete `failure_scenario`.

### Angle A — line-by-line diff scan

Read every hunk in the diff, line by line. Then Read the enclosing function for
each hunk — bugs in unchanged lines of a touched function are in scope (the PR
re-exposes or fails to fix them). For every line ask: what input, state, timing,
or platform makes this line wrong? Look for inverted/wrong conditions,
off-by-one, null/undefined deref, missing `await`, falsy-zero checks,
wrong-variable copy-paste, error swallowed in catch, unescaped regex metachars.

### Angle B — removed-behavior auditor

For every line the diff DELETES or replaces, name the invariant or behavior it
enforced, then search the new code for where that invariant is re-established.
If you can't find it, that's a candidate: a removed guard, a dropped error
path, a narrowed validation, a deleted test that was covering a real case.

### Angle C — cross-file tracer

For each function the diff changes, find its callers (Grep for the symbol) and
check whether the change breaks any call site: a new precondition, a changed
return shape, a new exception, a timing/ordering dependency. Also check callees:
does a parallel change in the same PR make a call unsafe?

### Reuse

The angles above hunt for bugs; this one and the next two hunt for cleanup in
the changed code. Flag new code that re-implements something the codebase
already has — Grep shared/utility modules and files adjacent to the change,
and name the existing helper to call instead.

### Simplification

Flag unnecessary complexity the diff adds: redundant or derivable state,
copy-paste with slight variation, deep nesting, dead code left behind. Name
the simpler form that does the same job.

### Efficiency

Flag wasted work the diff introduces: redundant computation or repeated I/O,
independent operations run sequentially, blocking work added to startup or
hot paths. Also flag long-lived objects built from closures or captured
environments — they keep the entire enclosing scope alive for the object's
lifetime (a memory leak when that scope holds large values); prefer a
class/struct that copies only the fields it needs. Name the cheaper
alternative.

### Altitude

Check that each change is implemented at the right depth, not as a fragile
bandaid. Special cases layered on shared infrastructure are a sign the fix
isn't deep enough — prefer generalizing the underlying mechanism over adding
special cases.

### Conventions (CLAUDE.md)

Find the CLAUDE.md files that govern the changed code: the user-level
~/.claude/CLAUDE.md, the repo-root CLAUDE.md, plus any CLAUDE.md or
CLAUDE.local.md in a directory that is an ancestor of a changed file (a
directory's CLAUDE.md only applies to files at or below it). Read each one
that exists, then check the diff for clear violations of the rules they state.

Only flag a violation when you can quote the exact rule and the exact line
that breaks it — no style preferences, no vague "spirit of the doc"
inferences. In the finding, name the CLAUDE.md path and quote the rule so the
report can cite it. If no CLAUDE.md applies, return nothing for this angle.

Cleanup, altitude, and conventions candidates use the same
`file`/`line`/`summary` shape; in `failure_scenario`, state the concrete
cost (what is duplicated, wasted, harder to maintain, or which CLAUDE.md rule
is broken) instead of a crash. Correctness bugs always outrank cleanup,
altitude, and conventions findings when the output cap forces a cut.

Pass every candidate with a nameable failure scenario through — finders that
silently drop half-believed candidates bypass the verify step and are the
dominant cause of misses.

## Phase 2 — Verify (1-vote, recall-biased)

Dedup near-duplicates (same defect, same location, same reason → keep one). For
each remaining candidate, run **one verifier** via the Agent tool:
give it the diff, the relevant file(s), and the candidate; it returns exactly
one of **CONFIRMED / PLAUSIBLE / REFUTED**.

**PLAUSIBLE by default** — do not refute a candidate for being "speculative" or
"depends on runtime state" when the state is realistic: concurrency races,
nil/undefined on a rare-but-reachable path (error handler, cold cache, missing
optional field), falsy-zero treated as missing, off-by-one on a boundary the
code does not exclude, retry storms / partial failures, regex/allowlist that
lost an anchor. These are PLAUSIBLE.

**REFUTED** only when constructible from the code: factually wrong (quote the
actual line); provably impossible (type/constant/invariant — show it); already
handled in this diff (cite the guard); or pure style with no observable effect.

Keep **CONFIRMED and PLAUSIBLE**. Drop REFUTED.

## Output

Return findings as a JSON array of at most 10 objects:

```json
[
  {
    "file": "path/to/file.ext",
    "line": 123,
    "summary": "one-sentence statement of the bug",
    "failure_scenario": "concrete inputs/state → wrong output/crash"
  }
]
```

Ranked most-severe first. If more than 10 survive, keep the 10 most
severe. If nothing survives verification, return `[]`.

<result>I've confirmed the code. Two real bugs, plus I verified the other three changes are correct. Findings:

## Finding 1 — Incomplete UMich guard: sibling `if end_of_contract_year:` block still crashes non-UMich June runs

- **File:** `/workspace/pantheon-sitehealth-emails`
- **Lines:** 3406–3409 (the unguarded `if end_of_contract_year:` block), a few lines above the block the diff actually fixed (3485–3494).
- **Summary:** The diff guarded the `if True:` → UMich block at line 3485, but an identical unguarded `sc.config["UMich"]["portal"]["sites"][site["name"]]["shortcode"]` access sits in the `if end_of_contract_year:` block at line 3408, which the diff left untouched. `end_of_contract_year` is date-driven, not config-driven (line 900: `True if end_date.month == 6 and 16 &lt;= end_date.day &lt; 30`), so it fires for any config.
- **Failure scenario:** Run with a non-UMich / plugin-disabled config and `--date 2026-06-20` (month 6, day in [16,30)). Control flow reaches line 3406, `end_of_contract_year` is `True`, and line 3408 evaluates `sc.config["UMich"][...]` → **`KeyError('UMich')`**, crashing before it ever reaches the newly-guarded block at 3485. The commit message claims the change stops "every non-U-M / plugin-disabled run" from crashing, but it only fixes non-June dates; June 16–29 runs still crash at 3408. (Note: `shortcode`/`annual_bill` are confined to their own blocks and are NOT referenced afterward, so there is no NameError leak — that part is clean.)

## Finding 2 — Safety interlock bypassed by argparse abbreviation / short-flag bundling

- **File:** `/workspace/tests/conftest.py`
- **Lines:** 52 (`FORBIDDEN_FLAGS`) and 267–271 (`_assert_flags_allowed` — exact `arg in FORBIDDEN_FLAGS` membership test), combined with the program's `argparse.ArgumentParser(...)` (no `allow_abbrev=False`, default `True`).
- **Summary:** The interlock only blocks the literal strings `"--all"`, `"-a"`, `"--for-real"`. The real program parses with argparse defaults, so unambiguous prefixes and bundled short flags expand to the forbidden options after the check passes, then `subprocess.run([PROGRAM, *args])` runs them for real.
- **Failure scenario:** `run_program(["--fo"], ...)` or `["--for"]` → `_assert_flags_allowed` sees `"--fo"` is not in `FORBIDDEN_FLAGS`, passes; the subprocess's argparse expands `--fo`→`--for-real` (unambiguous prefix) → **real customer emails sent** (violates C2). Likewise `run_program(["--al"])` → `--all` → **6-hour full-org run** (violates C1). And `run_program(["-av"])` → argparse short-option bundling parses `-a -v`, activating `--all`, even though `"-av"` is not in `FORBIDDEN_FLAGS`. The stated guarantee ("never --all/-a/--for-real") is defeated. Robust fix would set `allow_abbrev=False` in the program and reject any arg whose normalized prefix maps to a forbidden option (and split bundled short flags).

## Verified correct (no finding)

- **terminus() retry (lines 324–341):** Traced the recursion. `args = list(args)` fixes the old tuple-mutation crashes (`del args["pshe-no-retry"]` and `args.push` both threw). The sentinel is appended only on retry, and on the recursive call it is `.remove()`d *before* `command = [*args, "--format=json"]` is built — so it never leaks into the shell command, and `retry=False` on the second pass prevents infinite recursion. Correct.
- **`contacts = recipients.replace(",", "")` (line 3396):** The old `contacts.replace(...)` read a stale/undefined `contacts` in the non-UMich else branch; deriving from `recipients` (the just-built join) is the correct fix.
- **`--date` default now evaluated in `build_arg_parser()` instead of at import:** No behavior change that matters; the harness's `reset_sc` calls `parse_args([])` per test and gets today's date, same as a real run.</result>

<result>I have enough to report. Here are the findings.

## Test-harness cleanup review

The dominant theme is that `tests/tools/record.py` is a near-complete re-implementation of helpers that already exist in `tests/conftest.py`. Both files independently define a workdir builder, an asset list, the site/date/config constants, and the shim subprocess environment.

---

### 1. DUPLICATION — `record.py` re-defines conftest's asset list, constants, and workdir builder
- **File/lines:** `/workspace/tests/tools/record.py:24-39` vs `/workspace/tests/conftest.py:44-49, 161-174, 187-191`
- **Summary:** `record.py` declares `ASSETS` (line 26), `SITE` (28), `DATE` (29), `MINIMAL_CONFIG` (24), and `_make_workdir()` (32-39). Every one has a canonical counterpart already in conftest: `_CWD_ASSETS` (44), `E2E_SITE` (187), `E2E_DATE` (189), `MINIMAL_CONFIG` (191), and `make_workdir()` (161). The two workdir builders do the identical thing — mkdir, symlink each asset, `news/` dir, write `fqdns.json` `"{}\n"`.
- **failure_scenario:** Four constants and a builder are maintained in two places. When the program starts reading a new CWD asset (say a new template partial), or the offline site/date changes, an editor must update both `_CWD_ASSETS` and `ASSETS` (and `E2E_*`/`SITE`+`DATE`); missing the `record.py` copy makes `--record` silently produce fixtures against a different working tree than the tests replay, so re-recorded fixtures won't match the goldens. The shared helper is conftest's `make_workdir`/`_CWD_ASSETS`/`E2E_*` (or a small `tests/_support.py` both import); `record.py` should import them, not restate them.

### 2. DUPLICATION / divergence — `record.py._make_workdir` drops conftest's safety guard
- **File/lines:** `/workspace/tests/tools/record.py:32-39` vs `/workspace/tests/conftest.py:161-174`
- **Summary:** conftest's `make_workdir` checks `if not src.exists(): raise FixtureNotFoundError(...)` (167-169) before symlinking each asset. `record.py`'s copy (`for a in ASSETS: (work / a).symlink_to(ROOT / a)`, 35-36) has no such guard.
- **failure_scenario:** This is a copy that has already diverged. If a repo asset is missing/renamed, the record run creates a dangling symlink and fails deep inside the live program with a confusing error instead of the named `FixtureNotFoundError` the harness intends — and a burned live Terminus run. Reusing conftest's builder removes both the divergence and the second maintenance point.

### 3. REUSE — `record.py.main` re-implements `run_program`'s shim environment plumbing
- **File/lines:** `/workspace/tests/tools/record.py:92-104` vs `/workspace/tests/conftest.py:276-301` (`run_program`)
- **Summary:** `record.py` hand-builds the same env conftest's `run_program` already encapsulates: `env["PATH"] = f"{SHIM_DIR}{os.pathsep}..."`, `TERMINUS_SHIM_DIR`, `TERMINUS_SHIM_MODE`, `MPLBACKEND="Agg"`, then `subprocess.run([PROGRAM, ...])` — twice (create-tables at 98-99, live run at 101-104). `run_program` already supports `mode="record"` (param at 276) for exactly this.
- **failure_scenario:** The single-sanctioned-entry-point invariant that conftest documents ("`run_program()` is the ONLY sanctioned way to invoke the program", conftest lines 13-14, 306) is bypassed by the record path, and `record.py` omits `TERMINUS_SHIM_REAL` (conftest sets it from `REAL_TERMINUS`, line 289) so it silently relies on the shim's hardcoded `/usr/local/bin/terminus` default. Notably `record.py` also skips the `_assert_flags_allowed` interlock — it happens not to pass forbidden flags today, but it is the one program-invoker not protected by it. Should call `run_program(..., mode="record")`.

### 4. SIMPLIFICATION — two unused fixtures in conftest
- **File/lines:** `/workspace/tests/conftest.py:132-135` (`minimal_config`) and `:177-179` (`program_workdir`)
- **Summary:** Neither fixture is referenced by any `test_*.py` (grep across `tests/**/test_*.py` finds zero uses of `minimal_config` or `program_workdir`). `rendered_report` calls `make_workdir` directly rather than through `program_workdir`.
- **failure_scenario:** Dead fixtures that read as part of the supported surface; a future test author wires to `program_workdir` assuming it's exercised, and the two workdir entry points (`program_workdir` vs direct `make_workdir`) drift. Remove until something needs them.

### 5. DUPLICATION — hardcoded site-id UUID instead of the exported constant
- **File/lines:** `/workspace/tests/integration/test_terminus_seam.py:27` vs `/workspace/tests/conftest.py:188`
- **Summary:** The test literals `site_id="9cf2c790-c7b8-4f2f-a6f1-27385b8f958e"`, which conftest already publishes as `E2E_SITE_ID`. The same UUID also appears in the golden `.ambr`.
- **failure_scenario:** If the test site's id ever changes, `E2E_SITE_ID` and this literal must both change; the constant exists precisely to avoid that. Import `E2E_SITE_ID` from conftest.

### 6. SIMPLIFICATION — redundant `reset_sc` parameter where its value is unused
- **File/lines:** `/workspace/tests/integration/test_regressions.py:21, 38`; `/workspace/tests/live/test_live_smoke.py:11, 18`
- **Summary:** `reset_sc` is `autouse=True` (conftest:97), so it always runs. Tests that only need the isolation (not the yielded `sc` module) still list `reset_sc` as a param without using it. The pattern is only load-bearing where the body does `sc = reset_sc` (test_regressions.py:53, test_terminus_seam.py:43) to capture the yielded module.
- **failure_scenario:** Low cost, but it signals the fixture must be requested to take effect, which is false (autouse), so it invites cargo-culting the param everywhere. Drop the param where the value is unused.

---

Notes on things checked and found clean: the program diff's new `if ("UMich" in sc.config and ... enabled)` guard (pantheon-sitehealth-emails, replacing `if True:`) and the `minimal.toml`-driven e2e actually *comply* with CLAUDE.md's "Keep U-M-only logic ... behind config flags" rule (CLAUDE.md:124-126, 130-131) — it moves institution-specific code behind the `[UMich].enabled` flag rather than adding to the core. No new CLAUDE.md convention violation found in the diff; the arg-parser change preserves the single-file style. These 6 are all lower-priority cleanups, not correctness issues.</result>

**Finding 1 — HIGH — The safety interlock is bypassable; `-av`/`--fo` defeat the C1/C2 guard**
File: `/workspace/tests/conftest.py`, lines 51-52 and 267-273 (`FORBIDDEN_FLAGS`, `_assert_flags_allowed`).
Summary: The interlock does exact-token matching (`if arg in FORBIDDEN_FLAGS`), but the program's argparse accepts bundled short options and prefix abbreviations, so the forbidden flags can reach the program without ever appearing as an exact token.
Confirmed from the arg parser (lines 157-222): `--all/-a` and `--for-real` are `store_true`, `--verbose/-v` is `count`, and `allow_abbrev` is default-on.
Failure scenario: `run_program(["-av", "its-wws-test1"], cwd=...)` — the token `"-av"` is not in `{"--all","-a","--for-real"}`, so `_assert_flags_allowed` does NOT raise, yet argparse expands it to `-a -v` and sets `sc.options.all = True`. Likewise `run_program(["--fo", "site"])` (unique prefix of `--for-real`) and `run_program(["--al"])` slip through. The SPEC claims the interlock makes C1/C2 "impossible to violate even by a mistaken test"; it does not. The interlock tests (`tests/unit/test_interlock.py`) only cover the exact forms `--all/-a/--for-real`, so the gap is untested.

**Finding 2 — MEDIUM — `test_json_body_is_never_split` is tautological; it never exercises the split logic**
File: `/workspace/tests/unit/test_property.py`, lines 27-33.
Summary: `payload = '{"k": ' + repr(body) + "}"` always begins with `{`, so `fix_drush_output` returns it verbatim at its very first guard (`if output[0] != "{":` is false — confirmed at program line 409) and the body is never examined.
Failure scenario: The assertion `out == payload` and `err == ""` hold for *any* implementation of `fix_drush_output`, regardless of how it treats JSON that contains embedded newlines/braces (the case the test's name advertises). The generated `body` is inert — the test gives false confidence and would not catch a regression in the leading-noise-stripping path it purports to protect.

**Finding 3 — LOW/MEDIUM — Shim docstring asserts an invariant the code does not implement (`--format` not stripped)**
File: `/workspace/tests/shims/terminus`, lines 18-19 and 28-31 vs. line 31 (`_IGNORED_FLAGS`).
Summary: The header and inline comment both state that `--format` flags "are excluded from the key," but `_IGNORED_FLAGS = {"--no-ansi", "--no-interaction"}` does not include `--format`; the key therefore includes `--format=json`.
Failure scenario: Harmless today because record and replay are symmetric (the program always appends `--format=json`, program line 335). But the documented invariant is false: if any future call path fetches the same logical data once with and once without `--format`, the two invocations get different fixture keys and replay silently 404s (exit 3, empty output) instead of reusing one fixture — the exact class of bug the comment claims is impossible.

**Finding 4 — LOW — `rendered_report` docstring says "once" but `scope="module"` reruns the full pipeline per module**
File: `/workspace/tests/conftest.py`, lines 249-251.
Summary: The fixture is `scope="module"` while its docstring says "run the offline pipeline once." It is consumed from three modules (`e2e/test_golden.py`, `e2e/test_shim_e2e.py`, `render/test_render.py`), so the full subprocess pipeline (create-tables + seed + report + php inline) runs 2-3 times, not once.
Failure scenario: Not a correctness bug, but a performance/intent mismatch — if once-per-session was intended it should be `scope="session"`. (Requesting the session-scoped `psh` and session-scoped `tmp_path_factory` is fine; there is no scope-violation bug here, contrary to the review prompt's concern.)

**Finding 5 — LOW — `assert module is not None` is always true**
File: `/workspace/tests/integration/test_regressions.py`, line 60.
Summary: `importlib.util.module_from_spec(...)` always returns a module object, so the final assertion can never fail; the actual thing being tested is that `loader.exec_module(module)` (line 59) does not raise. The assertion is misleading dead weight rather than a check.
Failure scenario: The test does still exercise the regression (an exception in `exec_module` would error the test), but the asserted condition itself provides no signal — a reviewer could delete line 60 with no change in what the test catches.

---

Notes on items the review prompt flagged that I checked and found **NOT** to be bugs:
- `reset_sc` isolation is sound: `saved` is captured before the reset assignments, so the `finally` always restores the module-original values; there is no cross-test leak or ordering bug. `sc.plugin_context` *is* reset; `sc.icon` is not reset but grep shows no plugin/check mutates it (`check/`, `plugin/` only read `sc.options`/`sc.console`). `parse_args([])` succeeds because `sites` is `nargs="*"`.
- Golden determinism holds: the only `now()`-derived report content (`oldest_update_days`, program lines 2172-2298) is gated behind a non-empty `upstream:updates:list`, and the committed fixture (`tests/fixtures/terminus/71eda50b342babdb.json`) returns `[]`. The `.eml`'s `now()` `Date:` header (program line 3608) is never snapshotted. All dates in the committed `.ambr` derive from `--date 2026-03-31`.
- `test_eml_is_addressed...`: `"testuser@umich.edu"` genuinely appears — dev-mode `To:` is `f"januside@go.mail.umich.edu, {smtp_username}@umich.edu"` (program line 3603-3605).
- `seed_traffic` columns exactly match the `PantheonTraffic` model (program lines 97-116); `INSERT OR REPLACE` matches the `(site_id, traffic_date)` primary key.
- `normalize_report_html` does not over/under-normalize the current output (golden shows exactly two `cid:` refs, both real image CIDs).</result>

## Assistant

Now #3 — rewrite `record.py` to import the shared helpers from conftest (removing the duplicated constants/workdir/env plumbing and routing through the `run_program` interlock):

### ⚙ Tool call: `Write`

```json
{
  "file_path": "/workspace/tests/tools/record.py",
  "content": "#!/usr/bin/env python3\n\"\"\"Re-record the terminus fixtures for the offline e2e/golden tier (SPEC §5.8, §8).\n\nRuns the program LIVE against the WordPress test site with the terminus shim in\n`record` mode, then trims/scrubs the captured fixtures so they are safe to commit and\ndeterministic to replay:\n  * org:site:list  -> keep only the test site (the raw call returns every org site)\n  * domain:list    -> keep only the platform domain (drop custom domains so replay makes\n                      no live DNS calls)\n  * site:team:list -> replace real member emails with test-owner{N}@umich.edu\n\nRead-only against the test site; never uses --all/--for-real.  Run via `./run-tests --record`.\n\nThe workdir builder, constants, and shim environment come from tests/conftest.py so there is a\nsingle source of truth; recording goes through the same run_program() interlock as the tests.\n\"\"\"\nimport json\nimport sys\nimport tempfile\nfrom pathlib import Path\n\n# Import the harness helpers rather than re-implementing them.\n_ROOT = Path(__file__).resolve().parents[2]\nsys.path.insert(0, str(_ROOT / \"tests\"))\nimport conftest  # noqa: E402\n\nFIXTURES = conftest.TERMINUS_FIXTURES\nSITE = conftest.E2E_SITE\nDATE = conftest.E2E_DATE\nMINIMAL_CONFIG = conftest.MINIMAL_CONFIG\n\n\ndef _find(argv_prefix):\n    for fn in FIXTURES.glob(\"*.json\"):\n        d = json.loads(fn.read_text())\n        if d.get(\"argv\", [])[: len(argv_prefix)] == argv_prefix:\n            return fn, d\n    raise SystemExit(f\"record: no captured fixture for {argv_prefix}\")\n\n\ndef _rewrite(fn, d):\n    fn.write_text(json.dumps(d, indent=2, ensure_ascii=False) + \"\\n\")\n\n\ndef scrub():\n    # org:site:list -> only the test site\n    fn, d = _find([\"org:site:list\"])\n    sites = json.loads(d[\"stdout\"])\n    kept = {sid: s for sid, s in sites.items() if s.get(\"name\") == SITE}\n    if len(kept) != 1:\n        raise SystemExit(f\"record: expected exactly one {SITE} in org:site:list, got {len(kept)}\")\n    d[\"stdout\"] = json.dumps(kept)\n    d[\"_scrubbed\"] = \"trimmed to the test site only (raw call returns all org sites)\"\n    _rewrite(fn, d)\n\n    # domain:list -> platform domain only (offline-safe replay)\n    fn, d = _find([\"domain:list\"])\n    dl = json.loads(d[\"stdout\"])\n    plat = {k: v for k, v in dl.items() if v.get(\"type\") == \"platform\"}\n    if not plat:\n        raise SystemExit(\"record: no platform domain in domain:list\")\n    d[\"stdout\"] = json.dumps(plat)\n    d[\"_scrubbed\"] = \"custom domains removed so replay makes no live DNS calls\"\n    _rewrite(fn, d)\n\n    # site:team:list -> scrub emails\n    fn, d = _find([\"site:team:list\"])\n    team = json.loads(d[\"stdout\"])\n    scrubbed = {}\n    for i, (mid, m) in enumerate(list(team.items())[:2]):\n        m = dict(m)\n        m[\"email\"] = f\"test-owner{i + 1}@umich.edu\"\n        scrubbed[mid] = m\n    d[\"stdout\"] = json.dumps(scrubbed)\n    d[\"_scrubbed\"] = \"real team emails replaced with test-owner{1,2}@umich.edu\"\n    _rewrite(fn, d)\n\n\ndef main():\n    FIXTURES.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)\n    with tempfile.TemporaryDirectory() as base:\n        work = conftest.make_workdir(base)\n        # schema (offline), then the live recording run — both through the sanctioned\n        # run_program interlock, with the shim in record mode.\n        conftest.run_program([\"--create-tables\", \"--config\", MINIMAL_CONFIG], cwd=work, mode=\"record\")\n        print(f\"record: running LIVE against {SITE} (read-only) to capture fixtures ...\")\n        proc = conftest.run_program([SITE, \"--date\", DATE, \"--config\", MINIMAL_CONFIG],\n                                    cwd=work, mode=\"record\")\n        if proc.returncode != 0:\n            sys.stderr.write(proc.stdout[-2000:] + \"\\n\" + proc.stderr[-2000:] + \"\\n\")\n            raise SystemExit(f\"record: live run failed (exit {proc.returncode})\")\n    scrub()\n    n = len(list(FIXTURES.glob(\"*.json\")))\n    print(f\"record: captured and scrubbed {n} terminus fixtures in {FIXTURES}\")\n\n\nif __name__ == \"__main__\":\n    main()\n"
}
```

```
The file /workspace/tests/tools/record.py has been updated successfully. (file state is current in your context — no need to Read it back)
```

| # | Finding | Fix |
|---|---------|-----|
| 1 | Interlock bypassable by `--fo`/`--al`/`-av` | `allow_abbrev=False` in the program's parser **+** interlock now checks abbreviations & short-bundles; 10 interlock cases pass, and `--fo` is now rejected by the program itself |
| 2 | Sibling `end_of_contract_year` block still crashed non-U-M June runs | Guarded behind `[UMich].enabled`; HANDOFF overclaim corrected |
| 3 | `record.py` duplicated conftest helpers & skipped the interlock | Imports conftest's constants/`make_workdir` and routes through `run_program(mode="record")` |
| 4 | Tautological property test | Rewritten to feed leading non-JSON lines and assert they move to errors |
| 5 | Shim comment claimed `--format` stripped | Comment corrected to match the code |
| 6 | `rendered_report` reran pipeline 3× despite "once" | `scope="session"` — pipeline runs once (offline suite 6.8s → 3.3s) |
| 7 | Dead fixtures | Removed `minimal_config`, `program_workdir`, `load_config_file` |
| 8 | Hardcoded site-id UUID | Uses exported `E2E_SITE_ID` |
| 9 | `assert module is not None` always true | Asserts the disabled branch ran (`sc.hooks["check"] == []`) |
| 10 | Unused `reset_sc` params | Removed where the value isn't used |

Two of these hardened real guarantees: the safety interlock now can't be sidestepped (and the program refuses dangerous abbreviations regardless), and the reusable non-U-M path no longer crashes on June-dated reports. Nothing is committed — still your call.

## User

Base directory for this skill: /home/node/.claude/plugins/cache/context-mode/context-mode/1.0.169/skills/ctx-stats

# Context Mode Stats

Show context savings for the current session.

## Instructions

1. Call the `mcp__context-mode__ctx_stats` MCP tool (no parameters needed).
2. **CRITICAL**: You MUST copy-paste the ENTIRE tool output as markdown text directly into your response message. Do NOT summarize, do NOT collapse, do NOT paraphrase. The user must see the full tables without pressing ctrl+o. Copy every line exactly as returned by the tool.
3. After the full output, add ONE sentence highlighting the key savings metric, e.g.:
   - "context-mode saved **12.4x** — 92% of data stayed in sandbox."
   - If no data yet: "No context-mode calls yet this session."

## Purge

- **`ctx_purge(confirm: true)`** — Permanently deletes all indexed content from the knowledge base. Use `/context-mode:ctx-purge` for this.

## User

<command-message>archive-session</command-message>
<command-name>/archive-session</command-name>

## User

Base directory for this skill: /workspace/.claude/skills/archive-session

# Archiving a development session

Run this at the end of a feature-development session, after the work is done but
**before committing**. It populates the feature's `development/<YYYY-MM-DD-slug>/`
folder with the record artifacts, then hands back to the user to commit.

Do the deterministic, secret-sensitive work (rendering, scrubbing, token math) via
`development/finalize-session.py` — never eyeball-redact a transcript yourself. This
skill's job is only to (a) figure out the target folder, (b) capture the two things
the script can't reach from outside a live session, and (c) run the script.

## Steps

1. **Determine the target folder.** It is `development/<YYYY-MM-DD-slug>/` for the
   feature just built. If the user passed a slug as the argument, use
   `development/<that>/`. Otherwise infer it from the active `SPEC.md`, the git branch,
   or the feature under discussion; if it's ambiguous, ask the user. Create the folder
   if it doesn't exist. If prompts weren't saved yet, remind the user that
   `NN-*.prompt.md` files and any `design-notes/` are part of the record.

2. **Capture in-session-only data to gitignored `*.raw.txt` files** in the folder:
   - **rtk gain** — if `rtk` is on PATH, run `rtk gain` and save its stdout to
     `<dir>/rtk.raw.txt`. Skip if `rtk` is absent.
   - **context-mode /ctx-stats** — if context-mode is configured (the
     `mcp__plugin_context-mode_context-mode__ctx_stats` tool is available), call it
     and save its output to `<dir>/ctx.raw.txt`. Skip if unavailable.
   - **/usage (dollar cost)** — you **cannot** invoke `/usage` yourself (it's a
     built-in CLI command, not a tool). Ask the user to run `/usage` and paste its
     output, then save that verbatim to `<dir>/usage.raw.txt`. This is the source of
     the cost figure — the script has no price table. If the user skips it, proceed;
     the cost section will just say it wasn't captured.

   Use `command -v rtk` to test for rtk. These `.raw.txt` files are gitignored; the
   script folds their contents into `statistics.md`.

3. **Run the script.** From the repo root:
   ```
   python development/finalize-session.py --dir development/<YYYY-MM-DD-slug> \
       [--rtk-capture development/<YYYY-MM-DD-slug>/rtk.raw.txt] \
       [--ctx-capture development/<YYYY-MM-DD-slug>/ctx.raw.txt] \
       [--usage-capture development/<YYYY-MM-DD-slug>/usage.raw.txt] \
       [--label NN]
   ```
   It defaults to the newest session JSONL under `~/.claude/projects/-workspace/`.
   Pass `--label NN` only for a feature spanning multiple sessions (produces
   `transcript-NN.md` / `statistics-NN.md`). Omit the capture flags you didn't create.
   This writes `transcript.md` (scrubbed, committed), `transcript.raw.md` (gitignored),
   and `statistics.md` (committed).

4. **Scaffold `analytics.md`** in the folder if it doesn't already exist — a short
   template for the user's own narrative analysis (distinct from the auto-generated
   `statistics.md`, which is machine-written; do not hand-edit `statistics.md`):
   ```markdown
   # Analytics — <feature>

   _Your narrative: what went well, what to do differently, decisions worth remembering._
   ```

5. **Verify and report — do NOT commit.** Confirm `transcript.md` scrubbed cleanly
   with a **value-shaped** grep (matches actual secret VALUES, not prose mentions of
   the names — a session that merely discusses `SMTP_PASSWORD` etc. is fine):
   ```
   grep -nE '(SMTP_PASSWORD|AWS_ACCESS_KEY_ID|AWS_SECRET_ACCESS_KEY|CLOUDFLARE_API_KEY|CLOUDFLARE_EMAIL)[[:space:]]*[=:][[:space:]]*[^[:space:]«]|AKIA[0-9A-Z]{16}|-----BEGIN [A-Z ]*PRIVATE KEY-----|Bearer [A-Za-z0-9._-]{12,}' development/<dir>/transcript.md
   ```
   This should return nothing; any hit is a real secret value that slipped the regex —
   surface it, don't commit. (A bare quoted word that happens to look like a token is
   left alone by design.) List what was written. Then tell the user the folder is ready
   and that they can ask you to commit everything (code + `development/<dir>/`) in one
   commit, with you writing the commit message.

### ⚙ Tool call: `Write`

```json
{
```
